      <span itemprop="ratingCount" title="3139" class="value-title">3,139 Ratings</span>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14244009793997931912">In the old century, they called them the Gentry: ancient spirits of the land, magical, amoral, and dangerous. When the Irish emigrated to North America, some of the Gentry followed...only to find that the New World already had spirits of its own, called <em>manitou</em> and other such names by the Native tribes.<br /><p><br />Now generations have passed, and the Irish have made homes in the new l</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14244009793997931912">In the old century, they called them the Gentry: ancient spirits of the land, magical, amoral, and dangerous. When the Irish emigrated to North America, some of the Gentry followed...only to find that the New World already had spirits of its own, called <em>manitou</em> and other such names by the Native tribes.<br /><p><br />Now generations have passed, and the Irish have made homes in the new land, but the Gentry still wander homeless on the city streets. Gathering in the city shadows, they bide their time and dream of power. As their dreams grow harder, darker, fiercer, so do the Gentry themselves -- appearing, to those with the sight to see them, as hard and dangerous men, invariably dressed in black.<br /></p><p><br />Bettina can see the Gentry, and knows them for what they are. Part Indian, part Mexican, she was raised by her grandmother to understand the spirit world. Now she lives in Kellygnow, a massive old house run as an arts colony on the outskirts of Newford, a world away from the Southwestern desert of her youth. Outside her nighttime window, she often spies the dark men, squatting in the snow, smoking, brooding, waiting. She calls them <em>los lobos</em>, the wolves, and stays clear of them -- until the night one follows her to the woods, and takes her hand....<br /></p><p><br />Ellie, and independent young sculptor, is another with magic in her blood, bus she refuses to believe it, even though she, too, sees the dark men. A strange old woman has summoned Ellie to Kellygnow to create a mask for her based on an ancient Celtic artifact. It is the mask of the mythic Summer King -- another thing that Ellie does not believe in. Yet lack of belief won't dim the power of the mask, or its dreadful intent.<br /></p><p><br />Once again Charles de Lint weaves the mythic traditions of many cultures into a seamless cloth, bringing folklore, music, and unforgettable characters to life on modern city streets.<br /></p><p><br /><strong>Charles de Lint</strong> and his wife, artist MaryAnn Harris, live in Ottawa, Ontario.</p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14244009793997931912">...more</a>

      </div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_632018590">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/632018590" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4728718-algernon" class="left imgcol" title="Algernon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451037240p2/4728718.jpg" alt="Algernon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/632018590?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4728718-algernon" class="user" title="Algernon">Algernon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4728718-algernon?shelf=2013" class="actionLinkLite">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer632018590">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14403671353697753678">[7/10]<br />My third Newford book and probably not my last. I have not been reading them in order, but that's OK, as they can be enjoyed independently. I'm trading being more or less clueless about some of the recurring characters in order to focus on the ones particular to each novel as a stand-alone. <strong> Forests of the Heart </strong> refers to the notion of Home, the place, geographical as much as spiritual that defines and nourishes us, gives us strength and a feeling of continuity, of belonging to a history</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14403671353697753678">[7/10]<br />My third Newford book and probably not my last. I have not been reading them in order, but that's OK, as they can be enjoyed independently. I'm trading being more or less clueless about some of the recurring characters in order to focus on the ones particular to each novel as a stand-alone. <strong> Forests of the Heart </strong> refers to the notion of Home, the place, geographical as much as spiritual that defines and nourishes us, gives us strength and a feeling of continuity, of belonging to a history larger than our indivudual lives. <br /><br />The fictional city of Newport sits on the border. On one side are the Manitou, the native spirits who are being pushed away by the destruction of the forests and the expansion of the city. On the other are the Gentry - spirits from the Old World brought across the ocean by the Irish immigrants, adapted to urban lifestyle but trying to carve a realm of their own out of the <em> manido-aki / la epoca del mito </em>/ the spirit world. The myth of The Summer King / The Green Man / Lord of the Dance , of the period of summer and revelry being followed by winter and the need for a sacrifice that guarantees the return of spring is central to the story. Guy Gavriel Kay used a similar theme in The Fionnavar Tapestry. The meeting of these two cultures (native ans celtic) was seen in other Newford books. What I found of particular interest in this one is the introduction of a third strain : the Navajo / Mexican / Catholic heritage of the western desertlands, with its shapeshifters, herb-lore, milagros and especially the <em> cadejos </em> - another example of animal spirits in search of a home.<br /><br />One of the theories embraced by the author is that the artists are more open to the supernatural world than the common people, more ready to accept and to explore the realm of the fantastic. The setting of the book helps, as most of the action takes place around Kellygnow, an artist colony in a suburb of Newford. Ellie Jones is a sculptor who receives a comission from a mystery woman to carve a copy of an ancient mask. Her ex-boyfriend Donal is a painter who holds a grudge against society in general, likes to drink and gets mixed up with the Gentry. Bettina is part Indian part Mexican, an artist model and a mystical healer trained in the spiritual arts by her grandmother ( <em> abuela </em>). Donal's sister Miky works in a record store and in her free time she picks her accordion and plays in bars to both jazz and Irish folk music. Hunter is the owner of the record store, he gets caught in the plot almost by mistake, but rises to the occasion bravely. Tommy Raven is not an artist, but an Indian young man who provides the link to the Indian comunity through his formidable sixteen aunts. Tommy and Ellie in addition worl as volunteers in an organization that seeks to help the homeless of the big city, another nod at the central theme of the novel, of the need for a home and an identity:<br /><br /><em> They’re just people, Donal. More messed up than some of us, and certainly more unlucky. And if some of them choose to live the way they do, it’s not because they have some romantic story hidden in their past. It’s because they’re kids whose home lives were so awful they prefer to live in the different kind of hell that’s the streets. Or they’re schizophrenics who can’t get, or won’t take, their medicine. They’re alcoholics, or junkies, or on the run, or all of the above and then some. And the world they live in isn’t safe. It’s more dangerous than anything we can imagine. We go into it, but we can step back out whenever we want. They can’t. </em> <br /><br />Quite a large number of characters to follow around, but de Lint never falters in the development of the story, proving once again he is a master of the craft. I did have some issues with the author sometimes getting into lecture mode, preaching a sort of New Age gospel, and with the way things wrap up towards the end, when the feel good and think positive ethos kind of gets out of hand, but overall this is another successful treatment of the urban fantasy format. I believe Charles de Lint comes closer than any other author to Neil Gaiman when it comes to big concepts and with integrating diverse mythologies into a coherent imaginary world. But this impression may be helped along by the fact that I've also been reading <strong> The Sandman </strong> in parallel with this one.<br />I suggest to give a try to both of them:<br /><br /><em> “Little mysteries, they’re good for the soul.”<br /> “How so?”<br /> “They keep us guessing.”<br /> “And that’s a good thing?”<br /> “Well, sure. Mysteries break the patterns we impose upon the world — or maybe let us see them more clearly for a change.” </em><br /><br />A final comment about music: I find myself greatly attracted to the playlist provided by the author both in the introduction and all through the text. Not only am I OK with New Age records (Enya, Yanni, Keiko Matsui, etc), but I like to mix them with folk music, jazz, classical, rock and the occassional pop chart hits. Hunter's indie music shop reminded me of the friendly banter and the oddball characters hanging around the shelves in one of my favorite feelgood movies : <strong> Empire Records </strong> - so consider this as an added attraction for checking out the book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14403671353697753678">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer709226405">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17000154474476484907">What happens when people come over and take over? Well, we all know the answer to that question. But what happens to beliefs, to gods, to spirits? Charles de Lint answers that question in Forests of the Heart which deals with a conflict of spirits, both in the magical sense and the sense of self, in the town of Newford. It isn’t so much a question of good and evil, but more of a question what is the best thing to do, how does one make peace, what costs should be paid.<br /> The story takes place over</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17000154474476484907">What happens when people come over and take over? Well, we all know the answer to that question. But what happens to beliefs, to gods, to spirits? Charles de Lint answers that question in Forests of the Heart which deals with a conflict of spirits, both in the magical sense and the sense of self, in the town of Newford. It isn’t so much a question of good and evil, but more of a question what is the best thing to do, how does one make peace, what costs should be paid.<br />	The story takes place over a few days in the middle of a horrible winter storm. The characters are musicians, artists, and the inspiration. The conflicts are about creative energy, perhaps, but also about usage, power, and sorrow. It is a rather very moving novel. <br />	It will also add to your music rotation. Fair warning.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_280376">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280376" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/28516-erika" class="left imgcol" title="Erika "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1214825942p2/28516.jpg" alt="Erika " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/280376?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 30, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/28516-erika" class="user" title="Erika ">Erika </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/28516-erika?shelf=thefantastic" class="actionLinkLite">thefantastic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer280376">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18294562707850790254">I am a fan of Charles de Lint's short fiction, and in my opinion that is what he should stick to. He is clearly more adept at that form and length than he is at stretching a story to be novel-length. He skimped too much on details that I felt needed more clarification and breadth while overly emphasizing and rehashing other elements that I understood the first time around. The relationships between the characters and some of the characters themselves weren't terribly believable and seemed contri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18294562707850790254">I am a fan of Charles de Lint's short fiction, and in my opinion that is what he should stick to. He is clearly more adept at that form and length than he is at stretching a story to be novel-length. He skimped too much on details that I felt needed more clarification and breadth while overly emphasizing and rehashing other elements that I understood the first time around. The relationships between the characters and some of the characters themselves weren't terribly believable and seemed contrived (Donal's morose eeyore nature/act in particular REALLY annoyed me.) Another issue was the way in which he approached Bettina's bilingual dialog. I don't know any bilingual Spanish/English speakers that say something in Spanish and then immediately repeat it in English for all their gringo friends, and as someone who speaks Spanish it felt like I was reading the same phrase or sentence two times in a row. Then there were Donal and Miki constantly saying "Jaysus," because clearly if you're Irish you say that every other word.<br /><br />Regardless, the story was entertaining enough and I especially enjoyed the segments dealing with Bettina, even though Bettina repeating everything in English was annoying. I would definitely recommend one of his collections of short stories over this.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18294562707850790254">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1153501234">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1153501234" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7443303-anne" class="left imgcol" title="Anne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1326732411p2/7443303.jpg" alt="Anne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1153501234?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 14, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7443303-anne" class="user" title="Anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7443303-anne?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7443303-anne?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7443303-anne?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7443303-anne?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1153501234">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10253461816702662155">You know the kind of book where, even though you should be a responsible adult and put it down and go to sleep you cannot? And you stay up WAY too late just to see what happens? This book is THAT kind of book. <br /><br />I popped into the Newford series with this book having not read any of the other ones in the series before it, but I didn't find it disjointed. DeLint's writing is so good you can just immerse yourself in the world he's created and get to know the characters without needing any other back</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10253461816702662155">You know the kind of book where, even though you should be a responsible adult and put it down and go to sleep you cannot? And you stay up WAY too late just to see what happens? This book is THAT kind of book. <br /><br />I popped into the Newford series with this book having not read any of the other ones in the series before it, but I didn't find it disjointed. DeLint's writing is so good you can just immerse yourself in the world he's created and get to know the characters without needing any other back story. The book is filled with contrasts - the forest of Newford/the desert area where Bettina grew up, good/evil, light/dark, spirits/reality - and I loved the fact that the lines between all those contrasts are sometimes blurred and sometimes not. <br /><br />The concept of a place of the heart really spoke to me. Having moved around a lot both as a kid and in my adult life, finding that touchstone spot that feels like home is a really important thing. I fell in love with Bettina - such an old soul who has to walk thru fire in order to come to terms with who she is. She's such a strong character who ties all the contrasting parts together in a believeable way.<br /><br />I plan to go back and read the other 1-9 books, and will probably wind up reading the rest of his catalog as well. (Which my dad, who knows me very well, has been after me to do for years. No idea why I have waited so long.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10253461816702662155">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_49943246">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49943246" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1585377-lorina-stephens" class="left imgcol" title="Lorina Stephens"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442491926p2/1585377.jpg" alt="Lorina Stephens" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/49943246?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1585377-lorina-stephens" class="user" title="Lorina Stephens">Lorina Stephens</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49943246">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6031726827307330452">Charles de Lint is a master of urban fantasy. Combine that with his remarkable skill as a storyteller, his love of music, Celtic and Native legend and you have a tale that is enchanting, captivating, restorative. <br /><br />Forests of the Heart returns to de Lint's imaginary town of Newford, and draws heavily from native desert culture pitted against uprooted Celtic culture, all of it existing on an alternate plane that truly is just one step to the left. The Gentry, portrayed as angry, black-clad, cigaret</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6031726827307330452">Charles de Lint is a master of urban fantasy. Combine that with his remarkable skill as a storyteller, his love of music, Celtic and Native legend and you have a tale that is enchanting, captivating, restorative. <br /><br />Forests of the Heart returns to de Lint's imaginary town of Newford, and draws heavily from native desert culture pitted against uprooted Celtic culture, all of it existing on an alternate plane that truly is just one step to the left. The Gentry, portrayed as angry, black-clad, cigarette-smoking thugs, are used as dupes by a woman gifted in the ancient arts, who wants nothing more than to achieve immortality through the summoning of the Celtic green man, the Gladsuine. In turn, the Gentry dupe an angry young man into being the host for the summoning, and this, in turn, sets off a chain of events that take the reader from the deserts of Arizona to the ice-ravaged town of Newford. <br /><br />Always uplifting, often whimsical, Forests of the Heart is a delightful read I will likely return to again and again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6031726827307330452">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=faerie" class="actionLinkLite">faerie</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=art" class="actionLinkLite">art</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=mythology" class="actionLinkLite">mythology</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=folklore" class="actionLinkLite">folklore</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=canadian-literature" class="actionLinkLite">canadian-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=grandparents" class="actionLinkLite">grandparents</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=newford-series" class="actionLinkLite">newford-series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=brothers-and-sisters" class="actionLinkLite">brothers-and-sisters</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1020899-patty?shelf=artists" class="actionLinkLite">artists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer385667612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5134619481104015660">I am writing this review of de Lint's novel before I go and read the reviews I have written before. I love the world that de Lint has created; I feel like I have come home when one of his recurring characters appears in a new book; I just settle into his books like I belong there. The real question is why haven't I read all of them. Part of the reason is that I need to be in the right place in my mind and I also just want the time to enjoy them. I believe this is why I read them on vacation.<br /><br />This</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5134619481104015660">I am writing this review of de Lint's novel before I go and read the reviews I have written before. I love the world that de Lint has created; I feel like I have come home when one of his recurring characters appears in a new book; I just settle into his books like I belong there. The real question is why haven't I read all of them. Part of the reason is that I need to be in the right place in my mind and I also just want the time to enjoy them. I believe this is why I read them on vacation.<br /><br />This story takes place in Newford, de Lint's wonderful city, where magic and "real" life mix. If you read his books, the city will seem familiar and so will many of the characters. Even those people new to this story will obviously belong in Newford. The tale will be somewhat familiar, although for me, that is a big part of the charm. I know much of what will happen in a de Lint novel and that is why I read them. They are good, wonderful tales of what happens when Story (what some would define as magic or fairy tales) meets our reality. Given that Story is very important to me, I love every minute I am in Newford.<br /><br />I don't want to give away the plot of this particular book. If you read de Lint, you should know that his power as a storyteller is very apparent in this novel. If you have never encountered de Lint's fantasies, I think you should try a short story or two. Then if you are caught, pick any novel set in Newford. I don't think you will be disappointed.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5134619481104015660">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/673800919?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 05, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7402135-marlene" class="user" title="Marlene">Marlene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7402135-marlene?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer673800919">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17652107201515542713">DeLint, as always, has a triumphant story. Possibly my personal favorite DeLint novel simply because he weaves Native American people's myth with the myth of the Celts. He at once shows the differences in the myth and mysteries of the Native Peoples of the America's, (both Mexico and Southern U.S. which were at one point one in the same), and he shows us the beauty inherent in both along with its potential for malice. It is not lost that these are both human characteristics which each person and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17652107201515542713">DeLint, as always, has a triumphant story. Possibly my personal favorite DeLint novel simply because he weaves Native American people's myth with the myth of the Celts. He at once shows the differences in the myth and mysteries of the Native Peoples of the America's, (both Mexico and Southern U.S. which were at one point one in the same), and he shows us the beauty inherent in both along with its potential for malice. It is not lost that these are both human characteristics which each person and/or spirit must choose. <br /><br />In the beautiful manner of Delint's style, he presents to us an allegory of the European invasion of the Native People's land and their subsequent displacement. This theme is concurrent with the hope that both people and spirits now dwelling in the same continent can now choose to live in harmony, if we only choose to do so. I absolutely loved this book and would recommend this to anyone and everyone.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17652107201515542713">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer882483538">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8807333366610350916">Charles de Lint is a unique writer of contemporary fantasy, usually described as a writer of urban fantasy. I prefer his less "urban" books, and <em>Forests of the Heart</em> is my favorite among those. <em>Forests</em> returns to a theme that runs through many of his books: spiritual beings indigenous to the British Isles who somehow accompany emigrants to the Americas, where they interact with the people and indigenous spirits of America. <em>Forests</em> weaves a dark magic tale of Celtic and Southwestern Indian spirit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8807333366610350916">Charles de Lint is a unique writer of contemporary fantasy, usually described as a writer of urban fantasy. I prefer his less "urban" books, and <em>Forests of the Heart</em> is my favorite among those. <em>Forests</em> returns to a theme that runs through many of his books: spiritual beings indigenous to the British Isles who somehow accompany emigrants to the Americas, where they interact with the people and indigenous spirits of America. <em>Forests</em> weaves a dark magic tale of Celtic and Southwestern Indian spirit beings, and a young woman with extraordinary spiritual gifts. An unforgettable story about the power of human choices, and the ripple effects of even the smallest evil--and the smallest good.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1211387174">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12757660935803952186">Book #5 I've read from Charles de Lint. I wouldn't recommend this one. It felt very self-indulgent in the world-building details of Newford. Yes, I understand that he wants us to see this as a fully fleshed out, real town with many fascinating characters with the depth and complexity of real people. But do we need SO many characters in a book? Do we need to know the musical tastes of almost all of them? The book was so off-center. Starting it, I was hoping it would focus on Bettina and her deser</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12757660935803952186">Book #5 I've read from Charles de Lint. I wouldn't recommend this one. It felt very self-indulgent in the world-building details of Newford. Yes, I understand that he wants us to see this as a fully fleshed out, real town with many fascinating characters with the depth and complexity of real people. But do we need SO many characters in a book? Do we need to know the musical tastes of almost all of them? The book was so off-center. Starting it, I was hoping it would focus on Bettina and her desert magic. Her backstory was fascinating. Could have been a great standalone book. Instead, we have about 6 main characters with fully fleshed out stories and lives, in addition to a number of secondary characters. Way too many details make a book that takes too long to get going. By the time the action started to happen, I was so over this book. <br /><br />I won't give up on reading this author but I may have to give up on Newford as this is the second Newford book I found to be too long and badly edited. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12757660935803952186">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11246483832892834948">Hard men, the Gentry, Los Lobos, the Green Man,the Glasduine, Los Cadejos, Shaman, Wise Women, Shapeshifters, Los Santos, and very human humans...all here in a wonderfully imaginative narrative of magic, myth &amp; mystery. De Lint interweaves the myths of the Celts, Mexican Americans &amp; Native Americans into a story that takes place from a Northeastern city to a Southwestern desert - in the reality of the "now" and the realms of the spirit world. His characters are believable and interesting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11246483832892834948">Hard men, the Gentry, Los Lobos, the Green Man,the Glasduine, Los Cadejos, Shaman, Wise Women, Shapeshifters, Los Santos, and very human humans...all here in a wonderfully imaginative narrative of magic, myth &amp; mystery. De Lint interweaves the myths of the Celts, Mexican Americans &amp; Native Americans into a story that takes place from a Northeastern city to a Southwestern desert - in the reality of the "now" and the realms of the spirit world. His characters are believable and interesting. After reading this I will certainly read more of his work.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15006449776290847354">I have just re-read this, a long enough time had passed since the last reading that it was almost like reading it again.<br /><br />It is without a doubt urban fantasy, but with a difference. The different mythologies that make up the plot are bound with each other and with the story with De Lint’s typical deftness. The vivid engaging characters are the main strength of the novel as one sees through the eyes of different people and the people are distinct enough that you see a scene in different ways becaus</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15006449776290847354">I have just re-read this, a long enough time had passed since the last reading that it was almost like reading it again.<br /><br />It is without a doubt urban fantasy, but with a difference. The different mythologies that make up the plot are bound with each other and with the story with De Lint’s typical deftness. The vivid engaging characters are the main strength of the novel as one sees through the eyes of different people and the people are distinct enough that you see a scene in different ways because of the characters. The magic that some of the individuals possess are likewise distinct from each other, and the life paths of these different people and their own journeys within the book are very satisfying. While the main plot climax is satisfyingly large the book still leaves one with a feeling of a gentle story. I think for some people the ending may be less than satisfying as it leaves all the different people who were bound up in the climax to wander off in different directions into their own stories. I liked the ending myself.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_106333276">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106333276" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann" class="left imgcol" title="Althea Ann"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" alt="Althea Ann" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/106333276?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann" class="user" title="Althea Ann">Althea Ann</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer106333276">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17904111238113993929">Set in de Lint's imaginary modern American city of Newford (which seems a lot like Minneapolis to me, from the perspective of someone who's never been to Minneapolis...(it's cold, and it's not coastal)) tongue.gif<br />I have a feeling some of the characters have appeared in de Lint's other books as well, but I don't remember clearly enough to vouch for it.<br /><br />Here we meet Bettina, a Mexican/Native American who's been brought up in the mystic healing traditions by her grandmother, and who has long had an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17904111238113993929">Set in de Lint's imaginary modern American city of Newford (which seems a lot like Minneapolis to me, from the perspective of someone who's never been to Minneapolis...(it's cold, and it's not coastal)) tongue.gif<br />I have a feeling some of the characters have appeared in de Lint's other books as well, but I don't remember clearly enough to vouch for it.<br /><br />Here we meet Bettina, a Mexican/Native American who's been brought up in the mystic healing traditions by her grandmother, and who has long had an ambivalent relationship with dog spirits.<br /><br />Now, in Newford, a group of toughs who spend their time at the Irish pub, listening to Celtic music, drinking Guinness and beating people up, may be more than they seem... the 'hard men' are also known as 'los lobos' - the wolves, and they may be following an agenda of their own... a plan which may cast the spirit world into turmoil.<br />Bettina knows she must deal with the situation in some way...<br /><br />Into this mess are (mostly unwillingly) dragged: Ellie, a sculptor and volunteer who works with the homeless; her volunteer partner, Tommy, an ex-alcoholic Native American; Ellie's ex-, Donal, a grumpy and depressed Irishman, Donal's sister, Miki, a cheery hippie-punk musician, her boss at a record store, Hunter; Miki's co-worker, the goth chick Fiona... and an assortment of other characters.<br /><br />The plot centers around the 'hard men' and an art commission offered to Ellie that gets her into a prestigious artist's colony - but although the plot is fine, the book is more about spending time in de Lint's world, with his characters. He's consistently excellent as a writer at creating a social circle of people that by the end of a book, you feel you could be hanging out with later...<br /><br />That said, I also tend to feel that he tries just a tiny bit too hard to have his characters be 'hip,' to include representatives of disenfranchised or marginalized groups, and to include plugs for musical groups that he likes. That last is particularly problematic - a writer can talk about the emotional impact of a song on his characters, but if he insists on *telling* you that the song is by Ani DiFranco, and you happen to personally think that Ani DiFranco is whiny and irritating, it just rather spoils the effect.<br /><br />I have to also note, however, that de Lint does a much better job than nearly anyone else I can think of at writing fiction involving different ethnic spiritual traditions, and not having it come off as either cheesy or exploitative.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17904111238113993929">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer162452126">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1343417386311224402"><u>Forests of the Heart</u> is a lovely walk through the woods of the world. Another fabulous Newford tale by Charles de Lint, this one features a cast of characters ranging from Old World spirits, to New World sculptors and record-store-owners, to those with blood older than all of them. I will admit that at times the different sets of characters in canid form became somewhat challenging to tease apart as to their allegiances, but that's probably my own problem due to how quickly I was trying to get t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1343417386311224402"><u>Forests of the Heart</u> is a lovely walk through the woods of the world. Another fabulous Newford tale by Charles de Lint, this one features a cast of characters ranging from Old World spirits, to New World sculptors and record-store-owners, to those with blood older than all of them. I will admit that at times the different sets of characters in canid form became somewhat challenging to tease apart as to their allegiances, but that's probably my own problem due to how quickly I was trying to get through it :)<br /><br />The evil in this one is very palpable, as de Lint draws on mythology for quite an epic villain, though it's the humanity inherent in the Newford novels that really brings it home. I was impressed at how skillfully de Lint makes you sympathize quite a bit with the man who eventually brings about the existence of said villain, and then twists your sympathies once you realize what's really going on in his head. And I absolutely loved Bettina, the <em>curandera</em> who serves as the novel's main focus; her attempting to balance in many worlds is wonderfully melded with the mythology that the Newford novels have used before. I don't know if other Newford tales feature her or the others in <u>Forests of the Heart</u>, but if there are, I definitely want to read them!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1343417386311224402">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_656020983">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/656020983" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20196137-david-laderoute" class="left imgcol" title="David Laderoute"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1368120508p2/20196137.jpg" alt="David Laderoute" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/656020983?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 15, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20196137-david-laderoute" class="user" title="David Laderoute">David Laderoute</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer656020983">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5067674016920637675">I've long been a fan of Charles de Lint, ever since I first read Moon Heart in a bush camp back in the early 80s. He's a master of urban fantasy, much of it based around his imaginary city of Newford. Forests of the Heart takes us back there, this time in a story that crosses Celtic, Canadian Aboriginal and New World Spanish/SW American Native folklore.<br /><br />As usual, Charles gives us a great read. Forests is well-paced, with well-drawn, interesting characters (but...and there is a but, as I'll get to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5067674016920637675">I've long been a fan of Charles de Lint, ever since I first read Moon Heart in a bush camp back in the early 80s. He's a master of urban fantasy, much of it based around his imaginary city of Newford. Forests of the Heart takes us back there, this time in a story that crosses Celtic, Canadian Aboriginal and New World Spanish/SW American Native folklore.<br /><br />As usual, Charles gives us a great read. Forests is well-paced, with well-drawn, interesting characters (but...and there is a but, as I'll get to in a moment) and a compelling setting. Newford is hit by a massive ice storm (life imitating art as I write this, just a couple of weeks after Toronto and area was just whacked by the very same thing). The ferocious weather complicates matters for our heroes, who must contend with the inadvertent release of a ferocious monster based around the Green Man, an ancient nature spirit of life, death and rebirth. <br /><br />I have two problems with the story. First, I think Charles is trying to do too much, with too much material. He delves most deeply into the New World Spanish/SW American Native folklore, which is fascinating stuff--he brings that mythology to sparkling life. Unfortunately, his other two sources of spiritual magic, Celtic and Canadian Aboriginal, get shorted in comparison. I really like his take on the Gentry, aka the Hard Men, Celtic spirits who were dragged in chains of belief to North American by Irish immigrants and then essentially abandoned (echoes of Gaiman's American Gods). He portrays them as sullen, dangerous, cigarette-smoking men, which is a very cool take on ancient folklore. Trouble is, he doesn't do much with them, other than making them menacing and dangerous; he leaves them kinda flat. The Aboriginal Canadian folklore (a favorite of mine) gets even less attention, which is too bad; he doesn't quite evoke its nuances and textures and, again, leaves it rather superficial. I understand why--the book is long and complex enough. Still, I'd rather he'd perhaps omitted one of the mythologies and concentrated on the other two more, rather than focusing on a "three-sided" conflict.<br /><br />The other issue is related to too much folklore, and that's too many characters. These belief systems all have to be served through characters (and there's a actually a fourth belief system, which is anything that isn't the other three, including skepticism about myth and magic's existence at all). I found it had to keep track of characters and, frankly, wondered why some of them had been introduced in the first place, as they didn't really add much to the story.<br /><br />That said, I think Forests of the Heart is a fantastic read, and highly recommend it to anyone who loves contemporary and/or urban fantasy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5067674016920637675">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_244708437">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244708437" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7038421-isabel-kittiwake" class="left imgcol" title="Isabel (kittiwake)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1322770851p2/7038421.jpg" alt="Isabel (kittiwake)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/244708437?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 08, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7038421-isabel-kittiwake" class="user" title="Isabel (kittiwake)">Isabel (kittiwake)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1171449.Forests_of_the_Heart_Newford_Book_10_" title=" 9780575072947" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer244708437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6683207185655174826"><em>'So these wolves that come to our yard,' Bettina tried. 'En otros palabras - in other words. They are evil?'<br />Nuala shook her head. 'Not as you're using the word. Long ago, they followed the Irish emigrants to the New World, but this land already had its own guardian spirits. So there was no place for them. But here they remain all the same. They are homeless, unbound, and they neither feel nor think the way we do. When the Gentry gather in a pack they can be like a wild hunt, ravening and hungry</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6683207185655174826"><em>'So these wolves that come to our yard,' Bettina tried. 'En otros palabras - in other words. They are evil?'<br />Nuala shook her head. 'Not as you're using the word. Long ago, they followed the Irish emigrants to the New World, but this land already had its own guardian spirits. So there was no place for them. But here they remain all the same. They are homeless, unbound, and they neither feel nor think the way we do. When the Gentry gather in a pack they can be like a wild hunt, ravening and hungry for blood, but even on an individual basis, they're not to be trusted.'</em><br /><br />There are a couple of very stupid people in this book. For all their knowledge about the Gentry and other fairy folk, they have not grasped this one basic truth about the inhabitants of the spirit world. They are dangerous and untrustworthy and anyone who thinks that they will stick to their side of a bargain is a fool. Miki understands this and I am sure that even Chantal, whose only knowledge of such things comes from fairy tales she was told as a child, would too, so why don't they? <br /><br />Charles de Lint does irritate me quite a lot. In this book there is the way he has Bettina say a phrase in Spanish and immediately afterward repeat it in English, which gets tiresome quickly. And then there's the info dump about music since some of this book's characters work in a record shop. In the last book of his that I read the info dump was about guitar making since the protagonist was a luthier. But music and especially Celtic music seems to be an obsession of the author's. So your characters have great taste in music and are therefore cool and artistic and allowed to have contact with the spirit world. I get it! You can stop the constant name-dropping of musicians!<br /><br />But the story was good, and I did enjoy it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6683207185655174826">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_38073388">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38073388" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/41135-indiefishsteak" class="left imgcol" title="indiefishsteak"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1232162989p2/41135.jpg" alt="indiefishsteak" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38073388?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/41135-indiefishsteak" class="user" title="indiefishsteak">indiefishsteak</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38073388">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2743691496271539907">This is an inspiring and gritty adventure full of treks in to the otherworld and the spirits who inhabit both that world and this one. The beginning was a little slow for me, but once the characters started getting more intertwined with each other the stakes were raised. I really did not want to put it down toward the end.<br /><br />De Lint's writing has a beautiful way of sandwiching the urban and the supernatural into a wonderful blend of reality. Many of his books are in the city of Newford that he's cr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2743691496271539907">This is an inspiring and gritty adventure full of treks in to the otherworld and the spirits who inhabit both that world and this one. The beginning was a little slow for me, but once the characters started getting more intertwined with each other the stakes were raised. I really did not want to put it down toward the end.<br /><br />De Lint's writing has a beautiful way of sandwiching the urban and the supernatural into a wonderful blend of reality. Many of his books are in the city of Newford that he's created. The characters begin as slightly connected and eventually are all dependent on one another on what boils down to a monster hunt (though it's much more complicated than that, especially on an emotional level). They are all very different with varying backgrounds, a couple immigrants from Ireland with harsh histories, a recently broken-hearted music shop owner, a desert curandera (my personal favorite character), and a variety of spirits and friends. <br /><br />On a personal note, the character from the desert made me realize the things that I miss in New Mexico. How the desert speaks to you differently than anywhere else can. It is also a story of forgiveness and healing - which seems to be a common thread in de Lint's writing as far as I can tell. But I'm not complaining. It struck a chord with me, and I ran back to the store for another of his books: The Onion Girl.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2743691496271539907">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272371640" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6341900-indrani" class="left imgcol" title="Indrani"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1316314910p2/6341900.jpg" alt="Indrani" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/272371640?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6341900-indrani" class="user" title="Indrani">Indrani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer272371640">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer39543233498089424">This was classic de Lint: people in Newford with varying amounts of experience get caught up and drawn into the supernatural, and have to find ways to deal, and to fix the problems that they have (sometimes) inadvertently created or been part of.<br /><br />Much like Stephen King, I think that de Lint's success lies in his ability to create eminently relatable characters with motivations and emotions that connect with the reader; even the "bad guys" have motivations that makes sense. They may be more amoral</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText39543233498089424">This was classic de Lint: people in Newford with varying amounts of experience get caught up and drawn into the supernatural, and have to find ways to deal, and to fix the problems that they have (sometimes) inadvertently created or been part of.<br /><br />Much like Stephen King, I think that de Lint's success lies in his ability to create eminently relatable characters with motivations and emotions that connect with the reader; even the "bad guys" have motivations that makes sense. They may be more amoral than most of us, but it is possible to understand why they do what they do, and to wonder: if I hadn't learned to be a good person, if my life had been missing that connection with others, if I had felt beaten-up and abused, or throw away... could that be me? The good guys aren't always perfect; they make mistakes, do some soul-searching, question their choices. <br /><br />In any case, it was a quite enjoyable read, even if the themes were familiar stomping ground for me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="39543233498089424">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer140244562">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3763123778270733471">Another novel set in Newford, this time involving Irish wolf critters who want to displace the native Indian spirits and seize magical control of the land. The major human players this time are Bettina San Miguel, an Indian healer from the American s outhwest; Ellie Jones, an artist who works nights on aid to the homeless for "the Grasso Street Angel"; Tommy Raven, a Kickaha Indian; Hunter Cole, owner of Gypsy Records; his employee Miki Greer, and her brother Donal; and assorted Creek sisters, t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3763123778270733471">Another novel set in Newford, this time involving Irish wolf critters who want to displace the native Indian spirits and seize magical control of the land. The major human players this time are Bettina San Miguel, an Indian healer from the American s outhwest; Ellie Jones, an artist who works nights on aid to the homeless for "the Grasso Street Angel"; Tommy Raven, a Kickaha Indian; Hunter Cole, owner of Gypsy Records; his employee Miki Greer, and her brother Donal; and assorted Creek sisters, the aunts of Tommy Raven. Most of the heavy action takes place during the ice storm that shut down much of eastern Canada a few years ago.<br /><br />This is a de Lint Newford fantasy; each of the characters has to confront his or her own personal demons in uncomfortably real form, and either learn from the experience, or not. It's well done, and the language is very nice, and there's nothing here that de Lint hasn't done before. A satisfying but not significant book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18178280224358621785">As many other de Lint fans have voinced, the man needs to stick to short fiction.<br /><br />Once again the European fey realm clashes with Native American spirituality, a common theme of his stories. Not a bad thing, but it's a recurring theme of his.<br /><br />His female characters get a little predicable in this novel. You know, the innocent quite gal goes for the bad boy, etc. I don't understand the formula he uses to decide which character to give center stage and which to have in the background...this is because</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18178280224358621785">As many other de Lint fans have voinced, the man needs to stick to short fiction.<br /><br />Once again the European fey realm clashes with Native American spirituality, a common theme of his stories. Not a bad thing, but it's a recurring theme of his.<br /><br />His female characters get a little predicable in this novel. You know, the innocent quite gal goes for the bad boy, etc. I don't understand the formula he uses to decide which character to give center stage and which to have in the background...this is because he goes into <em>everyones</em> background in his novels. You can't tell which characters are supposed to be main and which are secondary. That would be my biggest complaint.<br /><br />However its most enjoyable aspect was a nearly new and fresh palette of characters, most of whom had never been featured in a previous Newford short story.<br /><br />At least de Lint isn't guilty of recycling the same kind of character under a different name and guise.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_38938755">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38938755" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/431794-amanda" class="left imgcol" title="Amanda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1191041954p2/431794.jpg" alt="Amanda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38938755?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 30, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/431794-amanda" class="user" title="Amanda">Amanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like to think the spirit world interacts with ours</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/431794-amanda?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38938755">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16790633979038652553">The plot of this book concerned the magical and mythical spirits of Ireland, Arizona, and New England, and a group of humans who got caught up in the spirit battle. I really enjoyed the character of Bettina - I felt she was well rounded and real. There were a lot of important supporting characters, though (somewhere around seven); this made it hard for me to remember who was who at the beginning of the book, especially as they were all interconnected and the book shifted from one point of view t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16790633979038652553">The plot of this book concerned the magical and mythical spirits of Ireland, Arizona, and New England, and a group of humans who got caught up in the spirit battle. I really enjoyed the character of Bettina - I felt she was well rounded and real. There were a lot of important supporting characters, though (somewhere around seven); this made it hard for me to remember who was who at the beginning of the book, especially as they were all interconnected and the book shifted from one point of view to the other. I also didn't like the author's writing style very much. He made me feel stupid when he would point out themes and such, especially when he had a character directly quote another character from earlier in the book. It really got on my nerves by the time I finished the book. All in all, I would give this book a 5 for plot, but a 2 for style, so it averages a 3.5.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16790633979038652553">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_113385830">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/113385830?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 07, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47313-linnea" class="user" title="linnea">linnea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/47313-linnea?shelf=girlswhodothings" class="actionLinkLite">girlswhodothings</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/47313-linnea?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer113385830">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15896670290991220502">This book didn't catch my attention as much as The Onion Girl did, but it was still fun to read. Charles De Lint's books, in my experience, have a very homey feel, people always dropping in on each other, going out for coffee or beers, having good food. And they're really about community, which I love. The actual story in this book was an interesting merging of Native American and Irish myth. What happens when Irish spirits come to the New World and have no home, no place of their own? Of course</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15896670290991220502">This book didn't catch my attention as much as The Onion Girl did, but it was still fun to read. Charles De Lint's books, in my experience, have a very homey feel, people always dropping in on each other, going out for coffee or beers, having good food. And they're really about community, which I love. The actual story in this book was an interesting merging of Native American and Irish myth. What happens when Irish spirits come to the New World and have no home, no place of their own? Of course they come into conflict with the spirits already there and then the characters have to work to bring back some kind of balance. Like I said, my favorite part is the community, and the discussions of the characters. The actually plot is kind of slow and winding. But also fun, it's all fun. You'll like it if you like Joseph Campbell.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_202625483">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202625483" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4313474-cupcakencorset" class="left imgcol" title="Cupcakencorset"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1284983423p2/4313474.jpg" alt="Cupcakencorset" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/202625483?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4313474-cupcakencorset" class="user" title="Cupcakencorset">Cupcakencorset</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer202625483">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4004820060435677797">This is one of my favorite de Lint novels so far. (Yes, I'm reading them in order. Is this a surprise to anyone? No, didn't think so.) The work includes some mythologies of Ireland, the Kikaha tribe and the deserts of the American southwest in a high-stakes collision. Family conflicts, loss and romances play out in a world where there is true magic in art, both old and new. The characters who live and act in this world (primarily set in Newford) are challenged to find their deepest wells of huma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4004820060435677797">This is one of my favorite de Lint novels so far. (Yes, I'm reading them in order. Is this a surprise to anyone? No, didn't think so.) The work includes some mythologies of Ireland, the Kikaha tribe and the deserts of the American southwest in a high-stakes collision. Family conflicts, loss and romances play out in a world where there is true magic in art, both old and new. The characters who live and act in this world (primarily set in Newford) are challenged to find their deepest wells of humanity when dealing with powers that are not at all human and with one another. If they cannot retain and act on that humanity, they will have lost, even if they win. It's this interplay of the personal and the mythical that make de Lint a master of urban fantasy. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4004820060435677797">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2Hm7I24Q8x9wi5IKLpnGvR/o1V09K7XJq5KUVpx7/k+9rYTwnMLn5fxT5rFQ+CAPVh8WRHT28mPBm5HEUO4ICg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9AkbJFQiHddXcvFxbJMe4BxEOWr5G5qIErA/lZ9KE4OR3ST3pvAJLduqhcoS8vhSVbP6c7DG3SJ4uToHU9/lxg==')})
  }

But a couple of years have passed and I guess maybe it\'s time to think about it again. Thus begins Ellen Pierson\'s story of how she helped her cousin Paul contend with the Malignant One running a temp agency in the office building where he worked. Ellen\'s story is a bright and moving tale set in the same fabulous, fantastic America as that of Rachel Pollack\'s award-winning Unquenchable Fire. Funny and frantic, poignant and powerful, Temporary Agency is an enduring fable from a writer whose work, in the words of Orson Scott Card, &amp;quot;like a river in flood, resists the well-channeled Many science fiction writers chronicling a vast technological shift lose sight of the people who would have to deal with it. Not so Kathleen Ann Goonan, whose Crescent City Rhapsody is the third of her Nanotech Cycle novels. Each of her characters is profoundly real, and the things that happen to them are as confusing, awe-inspiring, and terrifying as you might expect.  Goonan\'s story begins with the assassination of Marie Laveau, New Orleans cyber-entrepreneur and grand-niece of the famous voudoun queen. By prior arrangement, Marie is resurrected into a cloned body and prepares for revenge, but she awakens into a world beset by the Silence--periodic bursts of microchip-destroying radiation from space. Enter Dr. Zeb Aberly, a bipolar astrophysicist whose manic episodes help him understand that the Silence contains an alien message and perhaps the potential to change humanity\'s biology radically. Meanwhile, in Japan, a young biotechnician seals her fate when she helps steal the recipe for a Universal Assembler, a nanotech tool of fearsome power and destructive capability. The stage is set for a revolution, and Goonan delivers, with complex, interwoven story lines that resemble the rhythms and structure of a jazz composition.  Brightly colored lines were inching their way up buildings like plants in a fast-growing jungle. She moved briskly, but her heart was lifeless. She was looking at her past and seeing a future that she was not a part of. People sat leaning against buildings here and there, which was the hardest to see. They were not begging. Their brains were changing. They were adapting to the new city. As cities become organisms, a new generation of profoundly different humans comes of age and hope dawns in Crescent City, and Goonan directs the show with artistic flair. Crescent City Rhapsody is confusing and delightful, a swoony harmony of words swirling around crisply melodic ideas. --Therese Littleton&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"13534488567949617843\" Trickster characters have long been a staple of folk literature, and are a natural choice for the overarching subject of acclaimed editors Ellen Datlow and Terri Windling\'s third mythic anthology. The Coyote Road features a remarkable range of authors, each with his or her fictional look at a trickster character. These authors include Holly Black (The Spiderwick Chronicles), Charles de Lint (The Blue Girl), Ellen Klages (The Green Glass Sea), Kelly Link (Magic for Beginners), Patricia A. McKillip (Old Magic), and Jane Yolen. Terri Windling provides a comprehensive introduction to the trickster myths of the world, and the entire book is highlighted by the remarkable decorations of Charles Vess. Kate Wilhelm has done her usual excellent job of weaving an intricate plot &amp; sympathetically portraying believable &amp; complex characters in settings that are described with force &amp; clarity. This \'79 novel is set in&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText14769191794977246948\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Juniper Time is a 1st-rate sf novel. Kate Wilhelm has done her usual excellent job of weaving an intricate plot &amp;amp; sympathetically portraying believable &amp;amp; complex characters in settings that are described with force &amp;amp; clarity. This \'79 novel is set in the not-too-distant future, when a devastating drought in the American West &amp;amp; much of the rest of the world has caused economic &amp;amp; social collapse. The story alternates between the viewpoints of Cluny, a scientist dedicated to the construction &amp;amp; operation of a space station, &amp;amp; Jean, who was Cluny\'s childhood friend but has now gone her separate way &amp;amp; become a linguist, naturalist &amp;amp; photographer. Wilhelm\'s most powerful &amp;amp; engrossing writing, it seems to me, is in her descriptions of the natural world &amp;amp; of the vastly different ways that people relate to it. Jean\'s experiences on the Oregon coast are beautifully described, as is her life on the high desert of Oregon with the Wasco Indians. (Wilhelm &amp;amp; husband Damon Knight live in Bend) Jean gradually comes to understand the way of life of the Wasco people &amp;amp; her spiritual growth is described very effectively. Cluny &amp;amp; Jean are reunited when they become part of a project intended to discover if contact with an alien civilization has occurred. Their decision may determine whether a nuclear war between the USA &amp;amp; the USSR can be avoided. The climax of the novel is unexpected but believable. I recommend this book very highly.--Michael J.
